This confirms the proposed expression, demonstrating that the temperature-dependent expansion follows a predictable pattern consistent with fundamental thermodynamic transformations.

\subsection*{3. Numerical Validation}

To verify this equation, a numerical test will compute the ratio for various temperatures and compare the results with expected thermal expansion properties of atomic wavefunctions.

\begin{enumerate}
    \item Define \(\psi(r)\) and \(\psi_P(r)\) numerically, ensuring that the temperature dependence is incorporated properly.
    \item Compute the ratio across a range of temperatures \(T/T_0\), spanning from cryogenic conditions to elevated thermal states.
\item Compare the numerically computed values to the theoretical prediction, assessing the degree of agreement.
\item Analyze deviations to determine if additional corrections (such as higher-order thermal effects) are necessary.
\end{enumerate}

This validation serves as a test of whether vortex-induced thermal expansion in atomic orbitals aligns with known quantum-mechanical behavior and whether corrections to the standard model can be suggested. The comparison should also provide guidance on how experimental measurements of atomic expansion in plasmas or high-energy environments can be interpreted through the VAM framework.

\subsection*{4. Conclusion}

The derivation confirms the expected form of the temperature-dependent modification and supports the hypothesis that vortex structures influence quantum wavefunction behavior. Numerical tests will further confirm whether the functional form accurately captures the behavior of vortex-modified atomic structures in VAM. The incorporation of thermodynamic expansion principles into quantum wavefunction evolution offers a promising avenue for bridging classical and quantum perspectives on atomic structure. Future work should focus on comparing these theoretical predictions with spectroscopic measurements of atomic orbitals at different temperatures to assess the validity of the model under experimental conditions.

            \( \Phi \) & Vorticity-induced potential function, satisfying \( \nabla^2 \Phi = -\omega \). \\

            \( \lambda \) & Vortex core parameter, related to the characteristic decay length of vorticity. \\
            \( L \) & Rotational vortex core length \\

            \( \Psi_k \) & Vortex knot function describing topological structures in the Æther. \\
            \( \rho_\text{\ae} \) & Local Æther density, assumed to be incompressible in the model. \\
            \( P \) & Pressure in the Æther model, often governed by Bernoulli-like principles. \\
            \( H \) & Helicity, a measure of the knottedness of vortex tubes: \( H = \int \mathbf{v} \cdot \mathbf{\omega} \, dV \). \\
            \( K \) & Enstrophy, representing rotational energy density: \( K = \frac{1}{2} \int \omega^2 dV \). \\

            \( \mathbf{\Omega} \) & Angular velocity vector \\
            \( \mathbf{A} \) & Vector potential, where \( \mathbf{B} = \nabla \times \mathbf{A} \) in magnetohydrodynamic analogies. \\

    \section*{Validated VAM Equations}\label{sec:validated-vam-equations}
    \begin{equation*}
        \begin{array}{ccc}
            R_e = \frac{\lambda_c}{2 \pi} \alpha & R_e = \frac{e^2}{4 \pi \varepsilon_0 M_e c^2} & R_e = 2 R_c \\
            R_e = \alpha^2 a_0 & R_e = \frac{e^2}{4 \pi \varepsilon_c m_c c^2} & R_e = \frac{e^2}{8 \pi \varepsilon_0 F_{\max} R_c} \\
            R_x = N \frac{F_{\max} R_c^2}{M_e Z C_e^2} & e = \frac{\sqrt{16 \pi F_{\max} R_c^2}}{\mu_0 c^2} & e^2 = 16 \pi F_{\max} \xi_0 R_e^2 \\
            e = \frac{\sqrt{2 \alpha h}}{\mu_0 c} & e = \frac{\sqrt{4 \mathbf{v}_{\scriptscriptstyle\boldsymbol{\circlearrowleft}} h}}{\mu_0 c^2} & R^2 = \frac{N F_{\text {max }} R_c}{4 \pi^2 f^2 m_e} \\
            R^2 = \frac{4 \pi F_{\max} R_c^2}{C_e} \frac{1}{8 \pi^2 M_e f_e} & \frac{1}{R_c} = \frac{c^2}{a_0 2 C_e^2} & {L_p} = \sqrt{\frac{\hbar G}{c^3}} \\
            L_{\mathrm{planck}} = \frac{\lambda_e \mathbf{v}_{\scriptscriptstyle\boldsymbol{\circlearrowleft}} t_{\mathrm{planck}}}{2 \pi R_c} & L_\text{Planck} = \sqrt{\frac{\alpha_g \hbar R_c}{\mathbf{v}_{\scriptscriptstyle\boldsymbol{\circlearrowleft}} M_e}} & L_\text{Planck} = \sqrt{\frac{\hbar t_p^2 \mathbf{v}_{\scriptscriptstyle\boldsymbol{\circlearrowleft}} c^2}{2 F_{\max} R_c^2}} \\
        \end{array}
    \end{equation*}

    \begin{equation*}
    \begin{array}{ccc}
            G = \frac{\vec{C_e} c^3 l_p^2}{2 F_{\max } R_c^2} & G = \frac{\mathbf{v}_{\scriptscriptstyle\boldsymbol{\circlearrowleft}} c^3 t_p^2}{R_c m_e} & G = \frac{F_{\operatorname{max}} \alpha (c t_p)^2}{m_e^2} \\
            G = \frac{\mathbf{v}_{\scriptscriptstyle\boldsymbol{\circlearrowleft}} c L_\text{Planck}^2}{R_c M_e} & G = \frac{\alpha_g c^3 R_c}{\mathbf{v}_{\scriptscriptstyle\boldsymbol{\circlearrowleft}} M_e} & G = \frac{\mathbf{v}_{\scriptscriptstyle\boldsymbol{\circlearrowleft}} c^3 t_p^2}{R_c \frac{2 F_{\max} R_c}{c^2}} = \frac{\mathbf{v}_{\scriptscriptstyle\boldsymbol{\circlearrowleft}} c^5 t_p^2}{2 F_{\max} R_c^2} \\
            \alpha = \frac{\lambda_e}{4 \pi R_c} & \alpha = \frac{\mathbf{v}_{\scriptscriptstyle\boldsymbol{\circlearrowleft}} e^2}{8 \pi \varepsilon_0 R_c^2 c F_{\max}} & \alpha = \frac{\lambda_c}{4 \pi R_c} \\
            2\alpha^{-1} = \frac{\omega_c R_c}{C_e} & \alpha = \frac{\frac{c}{2 \alpha} e^2}{8 \pi \varepsilon_0 R_c^2 c F_{\max}} \implies \alpha^2 = \frac{e^2}{16 \pi \varepsilon_0 R_c^2 F_{\max}} & \alpha_g = \frac{2F_{\max} \mathbf{v}_{\scriptscriptstyle\boldsymbol{\circlearrowleft}} t_p^2}{\frac{2F_{\max} R_c^2}{C_e}} \\
            \alpha_g = \frac{C_e^2 t_p^2}{R_c^2} & \alpha_g = \frac{F_{\max} 2 \mathbf{v}_{\scriptscriptstyle\boldsymbol{\circlearrowleft}} t_p^2}{\hbar} & \alpha_g = \frac{F_{\text {max }} t_p^2}{a_0 M_e} \\
            \alpha_g = \frac{\mathbf{v}_{\scriptscriptstyle\boldsymbol{\circlearrowleft}} c^2 t_p^2 m_e}{\hbar R_c} & \alpha_g = \frac{C_e^2 L_\text{Planck}^2}{R_c^2 c^2} & M_e = \frac{2 F_{\max} R_c}{c^2} \\
        \end{array}
    \end{equation*}

    \begin{equation*}
    \begin{array}{ccc}
            f_e = \frac{C_e}{2 \pi R_c} & \lambda_c = \frac{2 \pi c R_c}{C_e} & \lambda_c = \frac{4 \pi F_{\max } R_c^2}{\mathbf{v}_{\scriptscriptstyle\boldsymbol{\circlearrowleft}} m_e C} \\
            M_e c^2 = 2 F_{\max } R_c & \lambda_c = \frac{2 \pi c R_c}{C_e} & \lambda_c = \frac{4 \pi F_{\max } R_c^2}{\mathbf{v}_{\scriptscriptstyle\boldsymbol{\circlearrowleft}} m_e C} \\
            \lambda_c = \frac{4 \pi R_c}{C_e} & \mathbf{v}_{\scriptscriptstyle\boldsymbol{\circlearrowleft}} = \frac{c}{2 \alpha} & R_c = \frac{R_e}{2} \\
            F_\text{centrifugal} \sim M_e R_c \left(\frac{C_e}{R_c}\right)^2 = \frac{M_e C_e^2}{R_c} & h = 4 \pi m_e \mathbf{v}_{\scriptscriptstyle\boldsymbol{\circlearrowleft}} a_0 & h = \frac{4 \pi F_\text {max } R_e^2}{C_e} \\
            h = \frac{16 \pi (F^{\text{max}}_{\text{\ae}})^2 R_c^3 a_0}{\hbar c^2} & R_\infty = \frac{C_e^3}{\pi R_c c^3} & \mathbf{v}_{\scriptscriptstyle\boldsymbol{\circlearrowleft}} = \frac{R_c M_e c^2}{\hbar} \\
            F_{\max} = \frac{1}{2} \left( \frac{C_e}{c} \right)^{-2} M_e \omega_c^2 R_c & F_{\max} = \frac{h \alpha c}{8 \pi R_c^2} & F_{\max} = \frac{e^2}{16 \pi \varepsilon_0 R_c^2} \\
    \end{array}
    \end{equation*}


\begin{equation*}
    u_\text{vortex}(r, \omega, T) = \frac{F^{\text{max}}_{\text{gr}} \omega^3}{\mathbf{v}_{\scriptscriptstyle\boldsymbol{\circlearrowleft}} r^2} \cdot \frac{1}{e^{\hbar \omega / k_B T} - 1}
\end{equation*}
\begin{equation*}
    s_\text{vortex}(r, T) = \frac{4 \pi^4 F^{\text{max}}_{\text{gr}} k_B^4 T^3}{45 \mathbf{v}_{\scriptscriptstyle\boldsymbol{\circlearrowleft}} r^2 \hbar^4}
\end{equation*}
\begin{equation*}
    \Phi_\text{vortex} = \frac{\pi^4 F^{\text{max}}_{\text{gr}} k_B^4 T^4}{15 \hbar^4 r}
\end{equation*}
\begin{equation*}
    u_\text{total}(T) \propto \frac{F^{\text{max}}_{\text{gr}} T^4}{\mathbf{v}_{\scriptscriptstyle\boldsymbol{\circlearrowleft}} r^2}
\end{equation*}
\begin{equation*}
    s_\text{total}(T) \propto \frac{F^{\text{max}}_{\text{gr}} T^3}{\mathbf{v}_{\scriptscriptstyle\boldsymbol{\circlearrowleft}} r^2}
\end{equation*}




\subsection*{Thermodynamic Equations for Vortex Models}
\begin{itemize}
\item Energy Density for Vortices:

\[
u_\text{vortex}(r, \omega) = \frac{F^{\text{max}}_{\text{gr}} \omega^3}{\mathbf{v}_{\scriptscriptstyle\boldsymbol{\circlearrowleft}} r^2}
\]
 Validated (dimensionally correct and matches blackbody radiation scaling)

\item Entropy Density for Vortices:

\[
s_\text{vortex}(r, \omega, T) = \frac{4 F^{\text{max}}_{\text{gr}} \omega^3}{3 T \mathbf{v}_{\scriptscriptstyle\boldsymbol{\circlearrowleft}} r^2}
\]
 Validated (consistent with thermodynamic entropy relations)

\end{itemize}
